{"nick":"joepie91","message":"for *all* checks, both multi-row and single-row checks, having the checks in your server code means that there's no check at the actual point of storage, which means that an external client (like the aforementioned \"other processes\") can insert data that, according to your server, would be invalid... but that then nevertheless exists","date":"2019-04-19T06:56:11.701Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"this can happen even if your application consists of multiple parts and they are not all upgraded exactly in sync, leading to one of the clients inserting data that would once have been valid but now is not anymore","date":"2019-04-19T06:56:33.077Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"because of these sort of edge cases, you want to have the validation defined as much as possible directly within the database that stores your data, because then you have the guarantee that there is no possible way, no matter what else goes wrong, to get data into the database without it having passed all the relevant validations","date":"2019-04-19T06:57:32.025Z","type":"message"}
